< review>
It was good to be able to dinehin now that COVID restrictions are lifted. We ordered from here 2 times during quarantine, and have been going here as our "go to" sushi place for the last 3 years.

The fish is fresh and the staff friendly. They have many unique rolls, 3 Amigos, Albacore Cilantro and if you are doing a keto diet, they have the Lollipop and several other options that will work for you.

They almost always have Blue Fin Tuna available. If you never tried it, spend the extra money and make your mouth happy.< /review>

< review>
My favorite neighborhood restaurant. With my favorite waitress friends. The food taste like sitting at the dinner table of any good authentic Mexican Family home. I like the chicken plate, chilaquiles, breakfast burritos, taco plate... with either your choice of al pastor, asada, or pollo... as well as the Mulitas etc. I've had just about everything on the menu. When we stayed in the area we went just about every week. Sometimes twice a week. The food is great, authentic, lite on the stomach, flavorful with great friendly service, in family oriented atmosphere. Anyone can order more than one thing in the menu and still not be extra full if you don't know your options on what to eat, and you won't get too weighted down if your a hungry eaters.  You will spend a lot less money than you think even if you order a few things on the menu.  Prices range from    $3 to less than$20, depending on what you're getting. The a variety of Mexican sweets, smooties, desserts etc. They make the best homemade refreshing Mexican flavored drinks, Waters and juices to quench your thirst during your tasty Mexican meal< /review>

<text>Been here a handful of times now and I'll continue to come back, let me tell you why. Limited seating but food comes quickly and people usually eat and leave.

This restaurant specializes in soba and udon noodles, hot and cold. There are a lot of combo options that include sushi, tempura, sashimi, and etc. My go-to combo is hot soba noodle soup with sashimi and plain rice.

Soba is healthier because it's made of buckwheat. Udon noodles are thicker that make the texture more interesting to chew.

Ample parking, the restaurant faces PCH and is on the side of Nijiya Market and BevMo. Visa and Mastercards are accepted. I'll be back soon enough!< /text>< UserId.>

< Review>
Our group was greatly confused by the tempura bowl combo and the ten zaru section which seemed like they offered the same dish expect the prices were a little off. So we did the only logical thing and ordered from both. We discovered the ten zaru came with dipping sauce for the tempura and the vegetables included unique vegetables like shiso leaf and shitake mushroom while the combo came with the typical vegetables and instead of a dipping sauce they put a sweet sauce on top. Another difference is they ten zaru came with vegetable rice instead of white rice. The soba portions were the same. Overall we had a good experience. The waitress was nice and attentive and the food was good.<//Review>

< text>
My biggest frustration is what I saw on the pictures and what I was served are two completely different things.

A decent restaurant with traditional cooking nothing that will surprise you.
I do recommend the butternut squash soup and I would stay away from the gazpacho.

The scallops were okay the garnish for the scallops was mediocre nothing exciting.

The service was very good! 5

What we had and rating out of 5

Housemade "EPI" Baguette 4
Can't go wrong with bread but it would have been terrific if served with balsamic and olive oil. Though that is more italian and not french.

Starters:

Deviled Eggs 3

Roasted Quail 4

Chilled Farmer's Market Melon Gazpacho 2

Fried Squash Blossom 4 if it has some kind of sauce it would have been a 5.

Heirloom Tomato Salad 2.5

Main:

Sauteed Scallops 3

Maple Leaf Duck Breast 2

Dessert:

Tahitian Vanilla Creme Brulee 2.5

Meyer Lemon Tartelette 4.5

The desserts were also okay the creme brulee was very thin and did not settle well as the cream was not as firm as I would like it it was a little watery.

Overall decent food very good service. If you're in the neighborhood you should stop by but I would not make any kind of detours to experience this.<//text>

< text>
This place is a valley landmark since the 60s. Service is always great, selection is top notch if they don't have it they will order it, and the prices are fair. Owner is very knowledgeable about products and skates himself. Not some corporate shop managed by people who Kno nothing about the product. My only problem with the place is the owner, Christian, is so easy to talk to, I always end up staying way longer than I intended to. Regardless, support your local skate shop. And hopefully they bring back skate demos in the parking lot one day...cuz that would be awesome. On a side note, they follow social distancing guidelines to the letter. I feel safe in there way more than any other retail shop I've been to.< /text>

<Name>Margie DeRose< /Name><date>1621314818541</date><rating>4</rating><review>I reserved a unit a couple of weeks before I needed it.  Unfortunately, the unit size I had reserved was not available when I showed up.  The staff was able to offer me a bigger unit at a great rate as an alternative.  I had never stored at a facility like this so it took some time to "get it" on how storage works in the city.  They have carts available for use, loading docks, freight elevators, and drive-in options for cars and mid-sized trucks.

My only concerns regarding this facility (and the reason for 4 stars and not 5) is that my access card did not allow me to exit the underground drive-in area with my card,  I had to use the call box each time.  It is a glitch with their system and I will update this review if the issue gets resolved.

The other issue is that their loading dock is not secure from a truck perspective...you need to have a spotter to keep an eye on your truck or lock it between each load...anyone could wander over from the nearby train tracks or road.  It's not a problem if you're prepared with a lock or spotter, just be aware.

Inside the facility is secure.  My unit felt very secure  inside the facility and protected from the elements.</review>< pics>

< review>
Edit:we recently switched from this vet. I was looking at our old bills and the have gone up more than 50
Im a tough sell when it comes to vets.  I just want one who makes decision based on logical analyses of the problem.  I have settled on Best Friends vet hospital.  They charge much less and don't try and upsell.  I had a long conversation with Dr. McCool when my pomeranian was first diagnosed with epilepsy and he gave me a thorough, well thought out, and logical plan to approach treatment.  We're sticking with best friends.<//review>

<user_id>115435850646997101573<//user_id>< user_name>
Edwin Park< /user_name>
< time>
1557391132544</time>
< Rating>
2</Rating>
< text>
I heard that Gogi Time was a good Korean BBQ place from a close friend, so I gave it a try and I was honestly so disappointed. The food and service were both lackluster and brought down the overall mood of my friend group. Here is why.

Lets start with the food. The food came in small portions (for a group of 5) and the quality of the meat was poor with fatty cuts. We had to cut out all the fat because it became too much in the end. We also ordered steamed egg as an appetizer and was absolutely disgusted when we scooped down to discover that the egg was barely cooked. When we showed this to our server, he merely brushed it off and said he would just add a new order of steamed egg to our next order. Our steamed egg failed to come and we had to ask again for the egg to come in at all. When the steamed egg did come in and was fully cooked, we tried it only to discover that it was too salty to even eat. We also ordered the soju cocktails and we could tell instantly that the soju wasn't the best quality because it was so hard to force down. Good soju is supposed to be smooth going down and have a crisp aftertaste but the cocktails here had a strange metallic taste to them. I believe in rating a restaurant based on the sole quality and taste of the food and this place gets a major disapproval from me.

Next is the service which doesn't affect my ratings but definitely impacts my experience and my mood towards this restaurant. Our server was barely present and rarely checked up on our table. We would eat and cook for 10 minutes and wait for 30 minutes just for the next set of meat to come in or to even get the server to take our order. When the server did get our order, he would constantly forget certain parts of our order and we would have to repeat it multiple times. Near the end we got fed up and just asked for the check because we were no longer in the mood to repeat ourselves or continue eating.

Overall Gogi Time fails to live up to the expectations that I have for Korean BBQ. For 30+ dollars and an additional 18% gratuity charge for any groups 5 or more, I feel that there are better options and the prices of the drinks here are overpriced considering the size and the quality of the drinks you receive.</text>

<Text>Gogi Time has great food, hands down! It's all-you-can eat, which means you won't leave hungry, and there are many different items on the menu to choose from. It's a busy place any day of the week, especially starting around 5:30 pm. You will need to allow some time to find parking because the lot is tiny with a limited number of spaces. The area seemed safe and it's  generally clean.

The staff is quite friendly, but they are so busy that they forget orders quite often. There were several different food items I requested and had to repeat the request sometimes as many as three times. I didn't really mind because all the employees are so cheerful and positive. Their workload is high level for sure.

I spent about $83, which included the tip and one libation for my partner. I've dined at Gogi twice already, and I expect to go there again in the near future.< /Text><pictures>None</pictures>< response>

< Text>
Sooo many options on the menu and it's great because it's all you can eat!
The meats were delicious and the variety of options for side dishes and soups were really great. It's been difficult to find a new korean bbq place I like in the bay area, but this is definitely one of my new favorites. The meat quality isn't amazing but it's great for the price you're paying.

The only con was that the service was slow, the order of meat we ordered never came so we sat with a hot grill for 10+ minutes before we realized they forgot about our order.

We also went a little early hoping to no have such a long wait time, we went at 6:30PM, they told us it would be a 30-40 minute wait, and it ended up being a 1.5hr wait instead.</Text>

106341461232749633943</UserId.>
<Name>Samuel Lemus<//Name><time>1527284565080</time>< Rate>
4< /Rate>
< text>
If you're ever in the mood for some ALL YOU CAN EAT [NOT DRINK] kbbq with lots of friends or family this is the place. Gogi time is a Kbbq location where you order several kinds of meat and you grill it until ready.

They offer such a wide variety of options and since this is all you can eat I recommend their potstickers.

The hours I've gone late on a weekend after 9pm are typically packed and with long lines so if you want to be seated quickly I recommend going before 8pm.

Parking is pretty abysmal with maybe 15spots for gogi time but there is street parking across the street.

In a way it reminds me of Doctor Who's TARDIS, from Outside this place looks pretty small and unappealing but inside it's so lively and large that you forget about it. I recommend coming with atleast a party of 4 otherwise the wait can be even longer due to their seating arrangement for the grill.<//text>

<user_name>Tu Lam</user_name><date>1409426667143<//date>< Rate>
4</Rate>
< Review>
It always starts with Wallace and him asking me "What's for lunch?"  Followed by "I don't know, what do you want?"  Then it always ends up being Korean or Sushi because he has to drive.  So the group is on the way for Korean food today, Pyeong Chang Tofu House, one of our regular places for Korean food.  We spot Gogi Time and said let's give it a try.  It was another Korean restaurant with a different name many years ago that I don't remember.  The place got a make over with new tables, new staff, new menu.  I got the Yuk Gae Jang which is spicy shredded beef soup.  My friend got the seafood tofu soup which he said was good, and our other friend got the spicy pork.  What I really like was that they provided lettuce to go with the spicy pork, most restaurants would charge for the lettuce, or it only comes when you get the BBQ (grill at the table).  The quantities are big here, and their Ban Chan (side dishes) came in larger plates than most people.   My bowl of soup was nice and spicy, it came with rice, but I couldn't eat much of it, it was just a lot of food.  What I like about this place is you can tell them who spicy you want your food.  I got medium, which was just right.

We were examining their all you can eat BBQ menu.  I was impressed that you could get appetizers as part of the BBQ meat. Most places you get the meat and the Ban Chan.  There was a table next to us that had ordered the BBQ and it looked good.  I think we're going to need to come back for the all you can eat BBQ for dinner.  They also have the hot pot in which you cook the meat in broth.< /Review>

<Text>Not the cheapest, just the best! The wait here can be unbearable but if you have a large party you can call ahead for a reservation. Although it's not written anywhere, the AYCE is two hours.  Year ago they use to use charcoal (which in my opinion) was more flavorful. Instead they switch to gas grills.

<Rating>5</Rating><Text>First time eating here.  Came for a friend's going away party.  Right near the West Grand/27th exit in Oakland.  First off, parking can be hard here as the restaurant shares a parking lot with a billiards and another bar/restaurant.  At night, you can park on the street during times when the parking meters are not enforced.  During my visit there, I only had the KBBQ and not the hot pot.  Grills were really nice.  They use cast iron grills so meats tend to not stick on the grills while cooking and don't need to be changed quite as often.  That is a plus in my opinion.  Ordered the spicy pork, bulgogi, thin sliced brisket, short rib tips, corn, zucchini,  rice cake and tofu soup.  Marinade on the meats tasted good and the slices were thick but thin enough to cook quick.  Good selection of banchan to eat while food was cooking on the grills.  The only criticism I have is the selection is not as extensive as Gen Korean BBQ which is roughly the same price for dinner.  Overall, the experience was good, service was speedy and attentive and the food was good (as long as the person cooking does it right!).< /Text><Pictures>None<//Pictures>< response>

The second you walk in, a blast of smokes hits your face, jacket, shirt, jeans and handbag.  You end up marinating in that smoke and come out smelling like Gogi Time.  Oh de la Gogi Time BBQ perfume.  You smell like original BBQ smoke!

For a party of 5 or more, you can entertain the idea of having both bbq grill pit and hot pot soup.  For less people, pick a poison.  My poison... bbq grill pit.

Talk about cinching  your eyebrows off, that's not a good way to do it or ever do it.

<text>$25/pp... for all you can eat hotpot or all you can eat BBQ. We did the hotpot and it included meats, ramens, dumplings, kimchi pancakes (they don't go into the hotpot), veggies... basically an extraordinarily extensive menu. All for $25. My San Francisco mind was blown and I kept looking for the fine print. Okay, they'll charge you if you don't finish the meat, but basically just don't be pathetic and finish your food. Also don't be a turd and order everything off the menu... unless you've had an especially grueling workout that day.

I'm used to going to Little Sheep Hotpot in SF, paying a la carte, and getting a bill of approximately $60-70/pp so I spent the meal beaming at my husband happily over the fact that I could order anything I wanted off the menu with impunity.

There are 6 main broths to choose from (we got half and half Mongolian spice and tom yom spice... which both tasted pretty unidentifiable from each other but were nice and spicy). I am a spice fiend, so I might ask for one to be extra spicy next time (both the soup and my face need to be bright fluorescent red before I'm fully happy).

Service was a bit scattered (it gets BUSY) but I absolutely enjoyed the meal. Pork and corn dumplings and the ribeye were particularly good.
Can't wait to go back. Next time... BBQ!<//text>< Pics>

<text>VERY popular korean barbecue place in Oakland. There is a parking lot (both front and back) and plenty of street parking. Come either early or late, before 6pm or after 9pm, if you don't want to wait an hour or more for a table. They got rid of the charcoal grilling, FYI.

AYCE is about $25 and comes with different kinds of meat (includes pretty decent kalbi), seafood, veggies, and various appetizers (like corn cheese, pancake, soondobu, japchae, potstickers). Service can be pretty shotty, which is my only complaint. There is a 2 hour limit, but you shouldn't need that long as the meat portions are pretty healthy, and they allow you to order up to 5 things at once. Get an order of the ssam platter for the garlic and soybean paste.

Banchan is pretty decent, but you have to ask to get refilled. Pro tip: the kimchi is muchly improved if you grill it.

As for meats, the kalbi, spicy marinated pork, pork belly, and perhaps bulgolgi is all you should really care to eat. The rest are just filler and mediocre.<//text><Pics>None< /Pics>< resp>

<Text>Tips:
- wear clothes you don't care about. You WILL smell like BBQ afterward
- note that they use charcoal grills, not gas

Pros:
- pretty good beef (bulgogi and spicy bulgogi were my favs)
- charcoal grills make the beef taste more BBQ-y than a gas stove
- good for large events (our 40+ people were seated in the back room)
- friendly staff who brought out all the dipping sauces and side dishes before we even thought to ask

Cons:
- grill stands above table, making it difficult to cook while seated
- charcoal is super hot and might make you tear up several times throughout the meal
- kimchi pancake is alright, but not like traditional Korean pancakes (it'll taste better if you grill it)
- $25 for all-you-can-eat KBBQ (compare to LA's average price of $20, before tax and tip)
- exhaust vents are practically useless
- you will smell like smoke and BBQ afterward (but that comes with any KBBQ)

Bottom line: This is one of the better KBBQ in East Bay. I still like LA KBBQ better (which is also cheaper), but I would probably come here again.< /Text><gmap_id>0x808f80ab0f1348a9:0x4923b85dffacff92<//gmap_id>< user>
105818373356803739204</user>
</record></dataset><record>

<userid>116796911158844589160< /userid><name>Noelle Ham</name><time>1392865117458</time>< Rating>
3< /Rating>
<Review>PSA: REALLY SMOKY INSIDE.

Came with a group of 6 to do the AYCE hot pot and bbq. We ordered the kimchi pancake to start, eh it was ok. Nothing special.

For the BBQ I was bummed there was no baby octopus. Or mussels. So the only thing I ate from the BBQ was chicken and squid. The rest of my party ordered tons of meats. For the hot pot we ordered a ton too!

Besides being completely out of a few of the menu items, the food was pretty good. I liked how they cook it on a charcoal rather than flame, so that can account for all the smoke in the restaurant...but still, SO SMOKY (I've never used this word so much in my life...)

However, the service was horrible. I understand it's a new restaurant (hence, the potential for being 4 stars...) but as of now, I'll keep it at 3. I guess being in the back room was a disadvantage because servers would forget we were back there. To the point where they'd come in looking at their cell phone, and then look up and be surprised people where eating.

There were multiple servers going in and out to try and place our orders, sometimes we'd get it quickly and other times servers would bring multiple things back. It was just slow. And when splitting the checks, it took a bit since the system (and servers) are all new. Then, they split the check's wrong. But it took long enough to get it so we just paid it.

But everyone was nice and friendly, so that's always a plus.

Note: They've also increased their prices! It's $25 for AYCE,  not $22.< /Review>< pics>
